### Post by Krishna_Kurup on 2013-10-05
Hi I'm extremely new to Ubuntu (and all Linux) so this is probably a ridiculously stupid question.  Im running Ubuntu 13.04 off a USB stick but it's not installed, I have an external hardrive I want to install it on but I want to be able to keep other files on it. Ive backed up everything on my external  so, after I install Ubuntu on it can I put those files back and still have access to them.


Also would it be possible to install to an SD card. I have an internal reader and an empty 32 GB SD  but when i got to the install menu It doesnt see the card.

Thanks in advance

---

### Post by heir4c on 2013-10-05
Welcome to Ubuntu forum,

For the external harddrive: Yes you can, but make more than one partition on that disk. 1 for install Ubuntu, the other you use it for that data. You need also a partition for a swap. So you need minimum 3 partitions.
(Or you can do a dualboot with Windows and use that external Hard drive for data/backup.)
Beware of the hardware you have on your system. I use old computers but in newer hardware there is a new system for the bootsector (UEFI) So, if you don't now what to do, wait for other people from this forum to inform you about that. I have no experience with that at the moment.

---

### Post by Krishna_Kurup on 2013-10-06
Alrite thank you

can you explain how to set up multiple partitions i've seen the part of the install where it lets you do this but I cant quite figure

---

### Post by heir4c on 2013-10-06
Maybe you do the partitioning with gParted (Partition Manager.) 
So stop the install and look via de Dash (UbuntuLogo on top of the Launcher on the left) for the GParted Partition Manager. Click on it.
You see something like this:

[IMG]http://i.imgur.com/UXBIoqO.png[/IMG]


On the right top you see a button. Click on it and you see your other Hard disk:


[IMG]http://i.imgur.com/roz9Z41.png[/IMG]


Select your second Hard disk and you see a different partition layout:


[IMG]http://i.imgur.com/8c21A6m.png[/IMG]


What you can do now is take screenshots of the 2 partition tables or open a terminal and typ in:

```
cfdisk
```

Select al the text inside with your mouse Copy it and post it here, so we see how the partitions are on this moment.

### Post by heir4c on 2013-10-06
you need to be root. use instead:
```
sudo cfdisk
```
or post a screenshot of the partitions viewed on gParted of your external disk.

### Post by mastablasta on 2013-10-07
the cf disk is not relaly helpful since it's showing /sda (internal disk)

so external disk drive is sdc and it only has one huge ntfs partition. you can install withouth any data loss on it.

- first defragment that drive (twice)
- next use windows disk manager to reduce the size of the NTFS part. the empty disk space is where Ubuntu will go. depends how much you want to decicate to the OS and how many applicaitons you want to install. But i find it that 20-30 GB is enough space to deal seriously with OS, but 8 GB is just about enough to fit the OS (but you can't install too many things there).
- time to run the installer. the options here are two:
----> select the disk you want to install to and then use largest empty disk space. but grub (bootloader that gives options to boot) will likely go to primary disk. if you have windows recovery disk you can repair the boot. i am not sure if this largest empty disk space option enables you to select where GRUB is installed.
----> a better option is to use something else, create your own linux partitions in the free disk space (/ and /swap)  and then tell the installer to install GRUB to /sdc (external disk). that way you just select the external drive to boot from in BIOS.

grub has to be on external drive, otherwise computer won't boot withouth the external drive plugged in. if this happens, it can easilly be repaired with windows recovery disk.

---
